<p>As Duke of York, Charles bore the <a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom">royal arms of the kingdom</a> <a href="/wiki/Cadency" title="Cadency">differenced</a> by a <a href="/wiki/Label_(heraldry)" title="Label (heraldry)">label</a> <a href="/wiki/Argent" title="Argent">Argent</a> of three points, each bearing three <a href="/wiki/Torteau" class="mw-redirect" title="Torteau">torteaux</a> <a href="/wiki/Gules" title="Gules">Gules</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAshmole1715532_340-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAshmole1715532-340">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> As the Prince of Wales, <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_the_Prince_of_Wales" title="Coat of arms of the Prince of Wales">he bore the royal arms differenced</a> by a plain label Argent of three points.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAshmole1715531,_534_341-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAshmole1715531,_534-341">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup> As king, Charles bore the royal arms undifferenced: <a href="/wiki/Quartering_(heraldry)" title="Quartering (heraldry)">Quarterly</a>, I and IV Grandquarterly, <a href="/wiki/Azure_(heraldry)" title="Azure (heraldry)">Azure</a> three <a href="/wiki/Fleur-de-lis" title="Fleur-de-lis">fleurs-de-lis</a> <a href="/wiki/Or_(heraldry)" title="Or (heraldry)">Or</a> (for France) and Gules three lions <a href="/wiki/Attitude_(heraldry)#Passant" title="Attitude (heraldry)">passant guardant</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pale_(heraldry)" title="Pale (heraldry)">pale</a> Or (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Arms_of_England" title="Royal Arms of England">for England</a>); II Or a lion <a href="/wiki/Rampant" class="mw-redirect" title="Rampant">rampant</a> within a <a href="/wiki/Tressure" class="mw-redirect" title="Tressure">tressure</a> flory-counter-flory Gules (<a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal coat of arms of Scotland">for Scotland</a>); III Azure a harp Or stringed Argent (for Ireland). In Scotland, the Scottish arms were placed in the first and fourth quarters with the English and French arms in the second quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJohnston190618_342-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJohnston190618-342">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Issue">Issue</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Five_Eldest_Children_of_Charles_I_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Five_Eldest_Children_of_Charles_I_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Five_Eldest_Children_of_Charles_I_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Five_Eldest_Children_of_Charles_I_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Five_Eldest_Children_of_Charles_I_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Five_Eldest_Children_of_Charles_I_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Five_Eldest_Children_of_Charles_I_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5167" data-file-height="4189" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Five_Eldest_Children_of_Charles_I_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Charles I's five eldest children, 1637. Left to right: <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Princess_Royal_and_Princess_of_Orange" title="Mary, Princess Royal and Princess of Orange">Mary</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">James</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Stuart_(1635%E2%80%931650)" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth Stuart (1635–1650)">Elizabeth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_England_(1637%E2%80%931640)" class="mw-redirect" title="Anne of England (1637–1640)">Anne</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Charles had nine children, two of whom eventually succeeded as king, and two of whom died at or shortly after birth.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir1996252–254_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir1996252–254-343">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886387087">.mw-parser-output table.ahnentafel{border-collapse:separate;border-spacing:0;line-height:130%}.mw-parser-output .ahnentafel tr{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ahnentafel-t{border-top:#000 solid 1px;border-left:#000 solid 1px}.mw-parser-output .ahnentafel-b{border-bottom:#000 solid 1px;border-left:#000 solid 1px}</style><div class="noresize"><table class="collapsible collapsed" style="margin:0.3em auto;clear:none;min-width:60em;width:auto;font-size:88%;border:1px solid #aaa"><tbody><tr><th style="padding:0.2em 0.3em 0.2em 4.3em;background:none;width:auto">Ancestors of Charles I of England<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELoudaMaclagan199927,_50_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoudaMaclagan199927,_50-345">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup></th></tr><tr><td style="text-align:center"><table class="ahnentafel" style="margin-left:auto; <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">All dates in this article are given in the <a href="/wiki/Julian_calendar" title="Julian calendar">Julian calendar</a>, which was used in Great Britain throughout Charles's lifetime. However, years are assumed to start on 1 January rather than <a href="/wiki/Lady_Day" title="Lady Day">25 March</a>, which was the English New Year until 1752.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Charles grew to a peak height of 5&#160;feet 4&#160;inches (163&#160;cm).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGregg198112_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGregg198112-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> </span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-79">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Rubens, who acted as the Spanish representative during peace negotiations in London, painted <i>Landscape with Saint George and the Dragon</i> in 1629–30.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGregg1981190–195_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGregg1981190–195-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The landscape is modelled on the <a href="/wiki/Thames_Valley" title="Thames Valley">Thames Valley</a>, and the central figures of <a href="/wiki/Saint_George" title="Saint George">Saint George</a> (England's <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a>) and a maiden resemble the king and queen.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The dragon of war lies slain under Charles's foot.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-90">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For example, James I ruled without Parliament between 1614 and 1621.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESharpe1992603_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharpe1992603-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> </span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-98"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-98">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For comparison, a typical farm labourer could earn 8d a day, or about £10 a year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEdwards199918_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdwards199918-97">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> </span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-105">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The statute forbade grants of monopolies to individuals but Charles circumvented the restriction by granting monopolies to companies.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-240"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-240">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Scots were promised £400,000 in instalments.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-299"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-299">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1813, part of Charles's beard, a piece of neck bone, and a tooth were taken as relics. They were placed back in the tomb in 1888.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Margaret-346"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Margaret_346-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Margaret_346-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">James V and Margaret Douglas were both children of <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Tudor" title="Margaret Tudor">Margaret Tudor</a>, the daughter of <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII of England</a>: James V by <a href="/wiki/James_IV_of_Scotland" title="James IV of Scotland">James IV of Scotland</a>, Margaret by <a href="/wiki/Archibald_Douglas,_6th_Earl_of_Angus" title="Archibald Douglas, 6th Earl of Angus">Archibald Douglas, Earl of Angus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELoudaMaclagan199927,_50_345-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoudaMaclagan199927,_50-345">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup> </span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Frederick_I-347"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Frederick_I_347-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Frederick_I_347-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Christian III and Elizabeth were both children of <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I_of_Denmark" title="Frederick I of Denmark">Frederick I of Denmark</a>: Christian by <a href="/wiki/Anna_of_Brandenburg,_Duchess_of_Mecklenburg" title="Anna of Brandenburg, Duchess of Mecklenburg">Anne of Brandenburg</a>, Elizabeth by <a href="/wiki/Sophia_of_Pomerania" class="mw-redirect" title="Sophia of Pomerania">Sophia of Pomerania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELoudaMaclagan199927,_50_345-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoudaMaclagan199927,_50-345">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup> </span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
